<p><i><b>Marvel's The Avengers</b></i><sup id="cite_ref-filmfestivaltraveler_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmfestivaltraveler-4">[4]</a></sup> (classified under the name <i><b>Marvel Avengers Assemble</b></i> in the United Kingdom and Ireland),<sup id="cite_ref-BBFC_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBFC-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IFCO_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFCO-5">[5]</a></sup> or simply <i><b>The Avengers</b></i>, is a 2012 American <a href="/wiki/Superhero_film" title="Superhero film">superhero film</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel Comics</a> superhero team <a href="/wiki/Avengers_(comics)" title="Avengers (comics)">of the same name</a>, produced by <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a> and distributed by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures</a>.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_1"><a href="#endnote_1">1</a></sup> It is <a href="/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films" title="List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films">the sixth film</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe">Marvel Cinematic Universe</a>. The film was written and directed by <a href="/wiki/Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon">Joss Whedon</a> and features an <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast" title="Ensemble cast">ensemble cast</a> that includes <a href="/wiki/Robert_Downey_Jr." title="Robert Downey Jr.">Robert Downey Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Evans_(actor)" title="Chris Evans (actor)">Chris Evans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ruffalo" title="Mark Ruffalo">Mark Ruffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hemsworth" title="Chris Hemsworth">Chris Hemsworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarlett_Johansson" title="Scarlett Johansson">Scarlett Johansson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Renner" title="Jeremy Renner">Jeremy Renner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hiddleston" title="Tom Hiddleston">Tom Hiddleston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clark_Gregg" title="Clark Gregg">Clark Gregg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobie_Smulders" title="Cobie Smulders">Cobie Smulders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stellan_Skarsg%C3%A5rd" title="Stellan Skarsgård">Stellan Skarsgård</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a>. In the film, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Fury" title="Nick Fury">Nick Fury</a>, director of the peacekeeping organization <a href="/wiki/S.H.I.E.L.D." title="S.H.I.E.L.D.">S.H.I.E.L.D.</a>, recruits <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man" title="Iron Man">Iron Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/Captain_America" title="Captain America">Captain America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hulk_(comics)" title="Hulk (comics)">Hulk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thor_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Thor (Marvel Comics)">Thor</a> to form a team that must stop Thor's brother <a href="/wiki/Loki_(comics)" title="Loki (comics)">Loki</a> from subjugating Earth.</p>
<p>The film's development began when Marvel Studios received a loan from <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a> in April 2005. After the success of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(2008_film)" title="Iron Man (2008 film)">Iron Man</a></i> in May 2008, Marvel announced that <i>The Avengers</i> would be released in July 2011. With the signing of Johansson in March 2009, the film was pushed back for a 2012 release. Whedon was brought on board in April 2010 and rewrote the original screenplay by <a href="/wiki/Zak_Penn" title="Zak Penn">Zak Penn</a>. Production began in April 2011 in Albuquerque, New Mexico, before moving to Cleveland, Ohio, in August and New York City in September. The film was converted to 3D in post-production.</p>
<p><i>The Avengers</i> premiered on April 11, 2012, at Hollywood's <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a> and was released theatrically in the United States on May 4, 2012. The film received positive reviews from critics, as well as <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Marvel%27s_The_Avengers" class="mw-redirect" title="List of accolades received by Marvel's The Avengers">numerous awards and nominations</a> including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA</a> nominations for achievements in visual effects. It has set or tied numerous box office records, including the <a href="/wiki/List_of_biggest_opening_weekends" class="mw-redirect" title="List of biggest opening weekends">biggest opening weekend</a> in North America. <i>The Avengers</i> grossed over $1.5 billion worldwide, and became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">third-highest-grossing film</a> during its theatrical run—as well as the first Marvel production to generate $1 billion in ticket sales. The film was released on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> and <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> on September 25, 2012. A sequel, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Age_of_Ultron" title="Avengers: Age of Ultron">Avengers: Age of Ultron</a></i>, was released on May 1, 2015, while two additional sequels, <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Infinity_War" title="Avengers: Infinity War">Avengers: Infinity War</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Untitled_Avengers_film" title="Untitled Avengers film">an untitled sequel</a>, are currently in development, with <i>Infinity War</i> scheduled for a May 4, 2018 release date, and its sequel scheduled to be released on May 3, 2019.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Asgard_(comics)" title="Asgard (comics)">Asgardian</a> <a href="/wiki/Loki_(comics)" title="Loki (comics)">Loki</a> encounters the Other, the leader of an extraterrestrial race known as the <a href="/wiki/Chitauri" title="Chitauri">Chitauri</a>. In exchange for retrieving the Tesseract,<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_2"><a href="#endnote_2">2</a></sup> a powerful energy source of unknown potential, the Other promises Loki an army with which he can subjugate Earth. <a href="/wiki/Nick_Fury" title="Nick Fury">Nick Fury</a>, director of the espionage agency <a href="/wiki/S.H.I.E.L.D." title="S.H.I.E.L.D.">S.H.I.E.L.D.</a>, and his lieutenant Agent <a href="/wiki/Maria_Hill" title="Maria Hill">Maria Hill</a> arrive at a remote research facility during an evacuation, where physicist Dr. <a href="/wiki/Erik_Selvig" title="Erik Selvig">Erik Selvig</a> is leading a research team experimenting on the Tesseract. Agent <a href="/wiki/Phil_Coulson" title="Phil Coulson">Phil Coulson</a> explains that the object has begun radiating an unusual form of energy. The Tesseract suddenly activates and opens a <a href="/wiki/Wormhole" title="Wormhole">wormhole</a>, allowing Loki to reach Earth. Loki takes the Tesseract and uses his scepter to enslave Selvig and a couple of agents, including <a href="/wiki/Hawkeye_(comics)" title="Hawkeye (comics)">Clint Barton</a>, to aid him in his getaway.</p>
<p>In response to the attack, Fury reactivates the "<a href="/wiki/Avengers_(comics)" title="Avengers (comics)">Avengers Initiative</a>". Agent <a href="/wiki/Black_Widow_(Natalia_Romanova)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Widow (Natalia Romanova)">Natasha Romanoff</a> is sent to <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Calcutta</a> to recruit <a href="/wiki/Hulk_(comics)" title="Hulk (comics)">Dr. Bruce Banner</a> to trace the Tesseract through its <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">gamma radiation</a> emissions. Coulson visits <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man" title="Iron Man">Tony Stark</a> to have him review Selvig's research, and Fury approaches <a href="/wiki/Captain_America" title="Captain America">Steve Rogers</a> with an assignment to retrieve the Tesseract.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>, Barton steals <a href="/wiki/Iridium" title="Iridium">iridium</a> needed to stabilize the Tesseract's power while Loki causes a distraction, leading to a confrontation with Rogers, Stark, and Romanoff that ends with Loki's surrender. While Loki is being escorted to S.H.I.E.L.D., <a href="/wiki/Thor_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Thor (Marvel Comics)">Thor</a>, his adoptive brother, arrives and frees him, hoping to convince him to abandon his plan and return to Asgard. After a confrontation with Stark and Rogers, Thor agrees to take Loki to S.H.I.E.L.D.'s flying aircraft carrier, the <a href="/wiki/Helicarrier" title="Helicarrier">Helicarrier</a>. There Loki is imprisoned while Banner and Stark attempt to locate the Tesseract.</p>
<p>The Avengers become divided, both over how to approach Loki and the revelation that S.H.I.E.L.D. plans to harness the Tesseract to develop weapons as a deterrent against hostile extraterrestrials. As the group argues, Barton and Loki's other possessed agents attack the Helicarrier, disabling its engines in flight and causing Banner to transform into the Hulk. Stark and Rogers try to restart the damaged engine, and Thor attempts to stop the Hulk's rampage. Romanoff fights Barton, and knocks him unconscious, breaking Loki's mind control. Loki escapes after killing Coulson and ejecting Thor from the airship, while the Hulk falls to the ground after attacking a S.H.I.E.L.D. fighter jet. Fury uses Coulson's death to motivate the Avengers into working as a team. Stark and Rogers realize that for Loki, simply defeating them will not be enough; he needs to overpower them publicly to validate himself as ruler of Earth. Loki uses the Tesseract, in conjunction with a device Selvig built, to open a wormhole above <a href="/wiki/Stark_Tower" title="Stark Tower">Stark Tower</a> to the Chitauri fleet in space, launching his invasion.</p>
<p>The Avengers rally in defense of New York City, the wormhole's location, but quickly realize they will be overwhelmed as wave after wave of Chitauri descend upon Earth. Banner arrives and transforms into the Hulk, and together he, Rogers, Stark, Thor, Barton, and Romanoff battle the Chitauri while evacuating civilians. The Hulk finds Loki and beats him into submission. Romanoff makes her way to the wormhole generator, where Selvig, freed of Loki's control, reveals that Loki's scepter can be used to shut down the generator. Meanwhile, Fury's superiors attempt to end the invasion by launching a nuclear missile at <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown Manhattan</a>. Stark intercepts the missile and takes it through the wormhole toward the Chitauri fleet. The missile detonates, destroying the Chitauri mothership and disabling their forces on Earth. Stark's suit runs out of power, and he falls back through the wormhole just as Romanoff closes it. Stark goes into freefall, but the Hulk saves him from crashing to the ground. In the aftermath, Thor returns Loki and the Tesseract to Asgard, while Fury expresses confidence that the Avengers will return if and when they are needed.</p>
<p>In a mid-credits scene, the Other confers with <a href="/wiki/Thanos" title="Thanos">his master</a><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_3"><a href="#endnote_3">3</a></sup> about the failed attack on Earth. In a <a href="/wiki/Post-credits_scene" title="Post-credits scene">post-credits scene</a>, the Avengers eat in silence at a <a href="/wiki/Shawarma" title="Shawarma">shawarma</a> restaurant.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Avengers_Cast_2010_Comic-Con_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Avengers_Cast_2010_Comic-Con_cropped.jpg/220px-The_Avengers_Cast_2010_Comic-Con_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Avengers_Cast_2010_Comic-Con_cropped.jpg/330px-The_Avengers_Cast_2010_Comic-Con_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Avengers_Cast_2010_Comic-Con_cropped.jpg/440px-The_Avengers_Cast_2010_Comic-Con_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1959" data-file-height="991" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Avengers_Cast_2010_Comic-Con_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cast of <i>The Avengers</i> at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon">Joss Whedon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Feige" title="Kevin Feige">Kevin Feige</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Downey_Jr." title="Robert Downey Jr.">Robert Downey Jr.</a> as <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man" title="Iron Man">Tony Stark / Iron Man</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A self-described genius, billionaire, <a href="/wiki/Playboy_(lifestyle)" title="Playboy (lifestyle)">playboy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Philanthropy" title="Philanthropy">philanthropist</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man%27s_armor" title="Iron Man's armor">electromechanical suit of armor</a> of his own invention. Downey was cast as part of his four-picture deal with Marvel Studios, which includes <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a></i> and <i>The Avengers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-RDJ_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RDJ-6">[6]</a></sup> Downey said that he initially pushed Whedon to make Stark the lead: "Well, I said, 'I need to be in the opening sequence. I don't know what you're thinking, but Tony needs to drive this thing.' He was like, 'Okay, let's try that.' We tried it and it didn't work, because this is a different sort of thing, the story and the idea and the theme is the theme, and everybody is just an arm of the octopus."<sup id="cite_ref-EW4_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW4-7">[7]</a></sup> About the character's evolution from previous films, Downey said, "In <i>Iron Man</i>, which was an origin story, he was his own epiphany and redemption of sorts. <i>Iron Man 2</i> is all about not being an island, dealing with legacy issues and making space for others. . . In <i>The Avengers</i>, he's throwing it down with the others".<sup id="cite_ref-Filmink_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Filmink-8">[8]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chris_Evans_(actor)" title="Chris Evans (actor)">Chris Evans</a> as <a href="/wiki/Captain_America" title="Captain America">Steve Rogers / Captain America</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> veteran who was enhanced to the peak of human physicality by an experimental serum and frozen in suspended animation before waking up in the modern world. Evans was cast as part of a deal to star in three Marvel films, in addition to <i>The Avengers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-9">[9]</a></sup> Evans said that Steve Rogers is much darker in <i>The Avengers</i>: "It's just about him trying to come to terms with the modern world. You've got to imagine, it's enough of a shock to accept the fact that you're in a completely different time, but everybody you know is dead. Everybody you cared about. . . He was a soldier, obviously, everybody he went to battle with, all of his brothers in arms, they're all dead. He's just lonely. I think in the beginning it's a fish-out-of-water scene, and it's tough. It's a tough pill for him to swallow. Then comes trying to find a balance with the modern world."<sup id="cite_ref-EW4_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW4-7">[7]</a></sup> Regarding the dynamic between Rogers and Tony Stark, Evans said, "I think there's certainly a dichotomy—this kind of friction between myself and Tony Stark, they're polar opposites. One guy is flash and spotlight and smooth, and the other guy is selfless and in the shadows and kind of quiet and they have to get along. They explore that, and it's pretty fun."<sup id="cite_ref-MTVNews10_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNews10-10">[10]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Ruffalo" title="Mark Ruffalo">Mark Ruffalo</a> as <a href="/wiki/Hulk_(comics)" title="Hulk (comics)">Bruce Banner / Hulk</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A genius scientist who, because of exposure to <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">gamma radiation</a>, transforms into a monster when enraged or agitated. Ruffalo, who was considered to play Banner in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Incredible_Hulk_(film)" title="The Incredible Hulk (film)">The Incredible Hulk</a></i> before <a href="/wiki/Edward_Norton" title="Edward Norton">Edward Norton</a> took the role,<sup id="cite_ref-CastRuffalo2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CastRuffalo2-11">[11]</a></sup> was cast after negotiations between Marvel and Norton broke down.<sup id="cite_ref-Ruffalo_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ruffalo-12">[12]</a></sup> About replacing Norton, Ruffalo said, "I'm a friend of Ed's, and yeah, that wasn't a great way for all that to go down. But the way I see it is that Ed has bequeathed this part to me. I look at it as my generation's <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet" title="Hamlet">Hamlet</a></i>." About the character, he said, "He's a guy struggling with two sides of himself—the dark and the light—and everything he does in his life is filtered through issues of control. I grew up on the <a href="/wiki/The_Incredible_Hulk_(1978_TV_series)" title="The Incredible Hulk (1978 TV series)">Bill Bixby TV series</a>, which I thought was a really nuanced and real human way to look at the Hulk. I like that the part has those qualities".<sup id="cite_ref-EW1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW1-13">[13]</a></sup> Regarding the Hulk's place on the team, Ruffalo said, "He's like the teammate none of them are sure they want on their team. He's a loose cannon. It's like, 'Just throw a grenade in the middle of the group and let's hope it turns out well!"<sup id="cite_ref-Kimmel_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kimmel-14">[14]</a></sup> This is the first production in which the actor playing Banner also plays the Hulk. Ruffalo told <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine, "I'm really excited. No one's ever played the Hulk exactly; they've always done CGI. They're going to do the <i>Avatar</i> stop-action, stop-motion capture. So I'll actually play the Hulk. That'll be fun".<sup id="cite_ref-NYMag_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYMag-15">[15]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/3D_modeling" title="3D modeling">3D model</a> used to create the Hulk's body was modeled after <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> bodybuilder and male stripper Steve Romm, while the Hulk's face was modeled after Ruffalo.<sup id="cite_ref-CastRuffalo1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CastRuffalo1-16">[16]</a></sup> To create the Hulk's voice, Ruffalo's voice was blended with those of <a href="/wiki/Lou_Ferrigno" title="Lou Ferrigno">Lou Ferrigno</a> and others;<sup id="cite_ref-soundworks_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soundworks-17">[17]</a></sup> however, the Hulk's only speaking line ("Puny god.") was provided solely by Ruffalo.<sup id="cite_ref-HulkVoice_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HulkVoice-18">[18]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chris_Hemsworth" title="Chris Hemsworth">Chris Hemsworth</a> as <a href="/wiki/Thor_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Thor (Marvel Comics)">Thor</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>The <a href="/wiki/Crown_prince" title="Crown prince">crown prince</a> of <a href="/wiki/Asgard_(comics)" title="Asgard (comics)">Asgard</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology">Norse mythological</a> deity of the <a href="/wiki/Thor" title="Thor">same name</a>. Hemsworth was cast as part of a multiple movie deal.<sup id="cite_ref-Hemsworth_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hemsworth-19">[19]</a></sup> He had previously worked with Joss Whedon on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cabin_in_the_Woods" title="The Cabin in the Woods">The Cabin in the Woods</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MTVNews7_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNews7-20">[20]</a></sup> Hemsworth said that he was able to maintain the strength he built up for <i><a href="/wiki/Thor_(film)" title="Thor (film)">Thor</a></i> by increasing his food intake, consisting of chicken breasts, fish, steak, and eggs every day. When asked exactly how much, Hemsworth said, "My body weight in protein pretty much!"<sup id="cite_ref-EOnline_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EOnline-21">[21]</a></sup> He remarked that Thor's motivation "is much more of a personal one, in the sense that it's his brother that is stirring things up. Whereas everyone else, it's some bad guy who they've gotta take down. It's a different approach for me, or for Thor. He's constantly having to battle the greater good and what he should do vs. it's his little brother there. . . I've been frustrated with my brothers at times, or family, but I'm the only one who is allowed to be angry at them. There's a bit of that."<sup id="cite_ref-EW4_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW4-7">[7]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scarlett_Johansson" title="Scarlett Johansson">Scarlett Johansson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Black_Widow_(Natalia_Romanova)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Widow (Natalia Romanova)">Natasha Romanoff / Black Widow</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A highly trained spy working for S.H.I.E.L.D.<sup id="cite_ref-Johannson_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johannson-22">[22]</a></sup> About the character and her relationship with Hawkeye, Johansson said, "Our characters have a long history. They've fought together for a long time in a lot of battles in many different countries. We're the two members of this avenging group who are skilled warriors – we have no superpowers. Black Widow is definitely one of the team, though. She's not in the cast simply to be a romantic foil or eye candy. She's there to fight, so I never felt like I was the only girl. We all have our various skills and it feels equal".<sup id="cite_ref-Filmink_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Filmink-8">[8]</a></sup> Regarding her training, Johansson said, "Even though <i>Iron Man 2</i> was 'one-for-them,' I'd never done anything like that before. I'd never been physically driven in something, or a part of something so big. For <i>The Avengers</i>, I've spent so many months training with our stunt team, and fighting all the other actors, it's crazy. I do nothing but fight—all the time."<sup id="cite_ref-Biskind_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biskind-23">[23]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Renner" title="Jeremy Renner">Jeremy Renner</a> as <a href="/wiki/Hawkeye_(comics)" title="Hawkeye (comics)">Clint Barton / Hawkeye</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A master <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">archer</a> working as an agent for S.H.I.E.L.D.<sup id="cite_ref-Renner_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Renner-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABCNews_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABCNews-25">[25]</a></sup> Renner said it was a very physical role and that he trained physically and practiced archery as much as possible in preparation.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-26">[26]</a></sup> About the role, Renner said, "When I saw <i>Iron Man</i>, I thought that was a really kick-ass approach to superheroes. Then they told me about this Hawkeye character, and I liked how he wasn't really a superhero; he's just a guy with a high skill set. I could connect to that."<sup id="cite_ref-Filmink_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Filmink-8">[8]</a></sup> Regarding Hawkeye's sniper mentality, Renner said, "It's a lonely game. He's an outcast. His only connection is to Scarlett's character, Natasha. It's like a left hand/right hand thing. They coexist, and you need them both, especially when it comes to a physical mission."<sup id="cite_ref-Filmink_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Filmink-8">[8]</a></sup> Renner said Hawkeye is not insecure about his humanity. "Quite the opposite, he's the only one who can really take down the Hulk with his [tranquilizer-tipped] arrows. He knows his limitations. But when it comes down to it, there has to be a sense of confidence in any superhero."<sup id="cite_ref-EW4_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW4-7">[7]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tom_Hiddleston" title="Tom Hiddleston">Tom Hiddleston</a> as <a href="/wiki/Loki_(comics)" title="Loki (comics)">Loki</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Thor's adoptive brother and nemesis, based on the Norse mythological deity of the <a href="/wiki/Loki" title="Loki">same name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hemsworth_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hemsworth-19">[19]</a></sup> About his character's evolution from the film <i>Thor</i>, Hiddleston said, "I think the Loki we see in <i>The Avengers</i> is further advanced. You have to ask yourself the question: How pleasant an experience is it disappearing into a wormhole that has been created by some kind of super nuclear explosion of his own making? So I think by the time Loki shows up in <i>The Avengers</i>, he's seen a few things."<sup id="cite_ref-HiddlestonInt1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HiddlestonInt1-27">[27]</a></sup> About Loki's motivations, Hiddleston said, "At the beginning of <i>The Avengers</i>, he comes to Earth to subjugate it and his idea is to rule the human race as their king. And like all the delusional autocrats of human history, he thinks this is a great idea because if everyone is busy worshipping him, there will be no wars so he will create some kind of world peace by ruling them as a tyrant. But he is also kind of deluded in the fact that he thinks unlimited power will give him self-respect, so I haven't let go of the fact that he is still motivated by this terrible jealousy and kind of spiritual desolation."<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter5_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter5-28">[28]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clark_Gregg" title="Clark Gregg">Clark Gregg</a> as <a href="/wiki/Phil_Coulson" title="Phil Coulson">Phil Coulson</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>An agent with S.H.I.E.L.D. who oversees many of the division's field operations.<sup id="cite_ref-Gregg_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg-29">[29]</a></sup> Gregg was cast as part of a multi-picture deal with Marvel.<sup id="cite_ref-Gregg2_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg2-30">[30]</a></sup> Gregg said his role was expanded in <i>The Avengers</i>: "[What] Agent Coulson had become in terms of the import of this particular story, and how important his job is in bringing the Avengers together, it kind of felt a little surreal, like somebody was playing a prank and that wasn't the real script. But it wasn't, it was the real thing, I got to show up and do that stuff, and it felt like such an amazing payoff to what the journey had been and the fact I had been doing it for five years."<sup id="cite_ref-Gregg3_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg3-31">[31]</a></sup> Gregg said Whedon provided insight into his character's backstory, particularly about Coulson being a fan of Captain America.<sup id="cite_ref-Gregg3_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg3-31">[31]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cobie_Smulders" title="Cobie Smulders">Cobie Smulders</a> as <a href="/wiki/Maria_Hill" title="Maria Hill">Maria Hill</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A high-ranking agent with S.H.I.E.L.D. who works closely with Nick Fury.<sup id="cite_ref-SmuldersCostume_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SmuldersCostume-32">[32]</a></sup> Smulders, whom Joss Whedon once considered for his <a href="/wiki/Wonder_Woman_in_other_media#Live_action_film" title="Wonder Woman in other media">unproduced live-action Wonder Woman film</a>, was selected from a short list of potential actresses including <a href="/wiki/Morena_Baccarin" title="Morena Baccarin">Morena Baccarin</a>. Smulders' deal would integrate her into nine films.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter3_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter3-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Variety3_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety3-34">[34]</a></sup> Regarding her preparation, Smulders said, "I hired this amazing black-ops trainer to teach me how to hold a gun, take me to a shooting range, how to hit, how to hold myself, how to walk and basically how to look. I don't do a ton of fighting in the movie, which is why I wasn't offered a trainer, but I wanted to look like I had the ability to."<sup id="cite_ref-HIMYM_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HIMYM-35">[35]</a></sup> On relating to the character, Smulders said, "I can relate to her being a mom and being a businesswoman and trying to work full-time and raising a family and having a career. We're asked to do a lot of things these days. I feel she is just all about her job and keeping things going."<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter4_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter4-36">[36]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stellan_Skarsg%C3%A5rd" title="Stellan Skarsgård">Stellan Skarsgård</a> as <a href="/wiki/Erik_Selvig" title="Erik Selvig">Erik Selvig</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>An astrophysicist and a friend of Thor under Loki's control, who is studying the Tesseract's power.<sup id="cite_ref-Expressen_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Expressen-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SSA_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SSA-38">[38]</a></sup> Regarding Loki's control over Selvig, Skarsgård said, "Well with the scene we did in <i>Thor</i>, it was like Loki, one way or the other, entered Erik's mind. And in Avengers, you will see more clarity in how Loki is using Erik's mind."<sup id="cite_ref-SSA_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SSA-38">[38]</a></sup> About his role, he said, "[My character] is of importance but the size of the role is not big."<sup id="cite_ref-SSA_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SSA-38">[38]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Nick_Fury" title="Nick Fury">Nick Fury</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>The director of S.H.I.E.L.D., who was revealed in previous films to be coordinating the "Avengers Initiative". Jackson was brought to the project with a deal containing an option to play the character in up to nine Marvel films.<sup id="cite_ref-Jackson_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-39">[39]</a></sup> Jackson said he does more in <i>The Avengers</i> than in any of the previous films: "You don't have to wait until the end of the movie to see me". About the role, Jackson said, "It's always good to play somebody [who] is a positive in society as opposed to somebody who is a negative. . . I tried to make him as honest to the story and as honest to what real-life would seem." Jackson compared the character to Ordell in <i><a href="/wiki/Jackie_Brown_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jackie Brown (film)">Jackie Brown</a></i>, calling him "a nice guy to hang out with. You just don't want to cross him".<sup id="cite_ref-BBCRadio_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCRadio-40">[40]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maximiliano_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Maximiliano Hernández">Maximiliano Hernández</a> reprise their roles from previous films as <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Potts" title="Pepper Potts">Pepper Potts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jasper_Sitwell" title="Jasper Sitwell">Jasper Sitwell</a>, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bettany" title="Paul Bettany">Paul Bettany</a> returns to voice <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Jarvis#J.A.R.V.I.S." title="Edwin Jarvis">J.A.R.V.I.S.</a> Frequent Whedon collaborator <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Denisof" title="Alexis Denisof">Alexis Denisof</a> portrays the Other, and <a href="/wiki/Damion_Poitier" title="Damion Poitier">Damion Poitier</a> portrays his master, <a href="/wiki/Thanos" title="Thanos">Thanos</a> (unnamed in the film), in a post-credit scene.<sup id="cite_ref-Poitier_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poitier-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Powers_Boothe" title="Powers Boothe">Powers Boothe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Agutter" title="Jenny Agutter">Jenny Agutter</a> appear as members of the World Security Council.<sup id="cite_ref-Boothe_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boothe-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Agutter_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agutter-43">[43]</a></sup> Avengers co-creator <a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee" title="Stan Lee">Stan Lee</a> has a cameo appearance in a news report. <a href="/wiki/Harry_Dean_Stanton" title="Harry Dean Stanton">Harry Dean Stanton</a> cameos as a security guard, and Polish film director <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Skolimowski" title="Jerzy Skolimowski">Jerzy Skolimowski</a> appears as <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Luchkov" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgi Luchkov">Georgi Luchkov</a>, Romanoff's interrogator.<sup id="cite_ref-Stanton_and_Skolimowski_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stanton_and_Skolimowski-44">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Enver_Gjokaj" title="Enver Gjokaj">Enver Gjokaj</a>, who later went on to play Agent Daniel Sousa in the series <i><a href="/wiki/Agent_Carter_(TV_series)" title="Agent Carter (TV series)">Agent Carter</a></i>, appears as a police officer.<sup id="cite_ref-Gjokaj_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gjokaj-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:33%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"It goes back to the very first incarnation of The Avengers, it goes to <a href="/wiki/Ultimates" title="Ultimates">The Ultimates</a>, it goes to everything about it. It makes no sense, it's ridiculous. There's a thunder god, there's a green '<a href="/wiki/Id_(Freud)" class="mw-redirect" title="Id (Freud)">id</a>' giant rage monster, there's Captain America from the 40s, there's Tony Stark who definitely doesn't get along with anybody. Ultimately these people don't belong together and the whole movie is about finding yourself from community. And finding that you not only belong together but you need each other, very much. Obviously this will be expressed through punching but it will be the heart of the film."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon">Joss Whedon</a>, director of <i>The Avengers</i>, about the film.<sup id="cite_ref-io9_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-io9-46">[46]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Avi_Arad" title="Avi Arad">Avi Arad</a>, the CEO of Marvel Studios, first announced plans to develop the film in April 2005, after Marvel Enterprises declared independence by allying with <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a> to produce a slate of films that would be distributed by <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Variety1_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety1-47">[47]</a></sup> Marvel discussed their plans in a brief presentation to <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> analysts; the studio's intention was to release individual films for the main characters—to establish their identities and familiarize audiences with them—before merging the characters together in a <a href="/wiki/Fictional_crossover" class="mw-redirect" title="Fictional crossover">crossover</a> film.<sup id="cite_ref-Cinematical1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cinematical1-48">[48]</a></sup> Screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Zak_Penn" title="Zak Penn">Zak Penn</a>, who wrote <i><a href="/wiki/The_Incredible_Hulk_(film)" title="The Incredible Hulk (film)">The Incredible Hulk</a></i> (2008), was hired by Marvel Studios to write the film in June 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-49">[49]</a></sup> In the wake of the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_Writers_Guild_of_America_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–2008 Writers Guild of America strike">2007–2008 Writers Guild of America strike</a>, Marvel negotiated with the <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">Writers Guild of America</a> to ensure that it could create films based on its comic book counterparts, including Captain America, <a href="/wiki/Ant-Man" title="Ant-Man">Ant-Man</a> and The Avengers.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-50">[50]</a></sup> After the successful release of <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(2008_film)" title="Iron Man (2008 film)">Iron Man</a></i> (2008) in May, the company set a July 2011 release date for <i>The Avengers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-SuperheroHype_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperheroHype-51">[51]</a></sup> In September 2008, Marvel Studios reached an agreement with Paramount—an extension of a previous partnership—which gave the company distribution rights for five future Marvel films.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Casting began in October 2008 with Downey's signing.<sup id="cite_ref-RDJ_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RDJ-6">[6]</a></sup> Though <a href="/wiki/Don_Cheadle" title="Don Cheadle">Don Cheadle</a> was also reported to be reprising his <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a></i> role of <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">War Machine</a> for <i>The Avengers</i>, he later stated that he did not think the character would appear in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-RDJ_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RDJ-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MTVNews9_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNews9-53">[53]</a></sup> At the same time, two major prospects occurred for Marvel: <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a> was brought in as an executive producer for the film,<sup id="cite_ref-RDJ_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RDJ-6">[6]</a></sup> and the company signed a long-term lease with Raleigh Studios to produce three other big-budget films—<i>Iron Man&#160;2</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Thor_(film)" title="Thor (film)">Thor</a></i> (2011), and <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_America:_The_First_Avenger" title="Captain America: The First Avenger">Captain America: The First Avenger</a></i> (2011)—at their <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Beach,_California" title="Manhattan Beach, California">Manhattan Beach, California</a> complex.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter2_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter2-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lou_Ferrigno" title="Lou Ferrigno">Lou Ferrigno</a>, who voiced Hulk in <i>The Incredible Hulk</i>, stated that he would be involved in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferrigno_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrigno-55">[55]</a></sup> In February 2009, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> signed a nine-picture deal with Marvel Entertainment to play Nick Fury in <i>Iron Man&#160;2</i> and other films.<sup id="cite_ref-Jackson_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-39">[39]</a></sup> In September 2009, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Norton" title="Edward Norton">Edward Norton</a>, who played Bruce Banner in <i>The Incredible Hulk</i> stated that he was open to returning in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-MTVNews_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNews-56">[56]</a></sup> The next month, executive producer Jon Favreau stated that he would not direct the film, but would "definitely have input and a say". Favreau also expressed concerns, stating, "It's going to be hard, because I was so involved in creating the world of Iron Man, and Iron Man is very much a tech-based hero, and then with <i>Avengers</i> you're going to be introducing some supernatural aspects because of Thor... [Mixing] the two of those works very well in the comic books, but it's going to take a lot of thoughtfulness to make that all work and not blow the reality that we've created".<sup id="cite_ref-MTVNews2_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNews2-57">[57]</a></sup> In March 2009, actress Scarlett Johansson replaced <a href="/wiki/Emily_Blunt" title="Emily Blunt">Emily Blunt</a> in portraying Natasha Romanoff in <i>Iron Man 2</i>, a deal that subsequently attached her to <i>The Avengers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Johannson_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johannson-22">[22]</a></sup> The female superhero <a href="/wiki/Wasp_(comics)" title="Wasp (comics)">Wasp</a> was included in an earlier draft of the script written before Johansson's involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-sacks20120429_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sacks20120429-58">[58]</a></sup> The following day, Marvel announced that the film's release date had been pushed back to May 4, 2012, almost a full year later.<sup id="cite_ref-Cinematical3_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cinematical3-59">[59]</a></sup> Chris Hemsworth and Tom Hiddleston joined the film's cast in June, returning as Thor and Loki, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Hemsworth_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hemsworth-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2009, Penn talked about the crossover process, stating, "My job is to kind of shuttle between the different movies and make sure that finally we're mimicking that comic book structure where all of these movies are connected. . . There's just a board that tracks 'Here's where everything that happens in this movie overlaps with that movie'. . . I'm pushing them to do as many animatics as possible to animate the movie, to draw boards so that we're all working off the same visual ideas. But the exigencies of production take first priority".<sup id="cite_ref-CraveOnline_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CraveOnline-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2010, Marvel Studios chief <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Feige" title="Kevin Feige">Kevin Feige</a> was asked if it would be difficult to meld the fantasy of <i>Thor</i> with the high-tech science fiction in <i>Iron Man</i> and <i>The Avengers</i>. "No," he said, "because we're doing the <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kirby" title="Jack Kirby">Jack Kirby</a>/Stan Lee/<a href="/wiki/Walt_Simonson" title="Walt Simonson">Walt Simonson</a>/<a href="/wiki/J._Michael_Straczynski" title="J. Michael Straczynski">J. Michael Straczynski</a> <i>Thor</i>. We're not doing the blow-the-dust-off-of-the-old-Norse-book-in-your-library <i>Thor</i>. And in the <i>Thor</i> of the Marvel Universe, there's a race called the Asgardians. And we're linked through this Tree of Life that we're unaware of. It's real science, but we don't know about it yet. The 'Thor' movie is about teaching people that".<sup id="cite_ref-SuperheroHype2_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperheroHype2-61">[61]</a></sup> In March, it was reported that Penn had completed the first draft of the script, and that Marvel editor-in-chief <a href="/wiki/Joe_Quesada" title="Joe Quesada">Joe Quesada</a> and <i>Avengers</i> comic-book writer <a href="/wiki/Brian_Michael_Bendis" title="Brian Michael Bendis">Brian Michael Bendis</a> had received copies.<sup id="cite_ref-MTVNews3_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNews3-62">[62]</a></sup> Also in March, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Evans_(actor)" title="Chris Evans (actor)">Chris Evans</a> accepted an offer to play Captain America in three films including <i>The Avengers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-production">Pre-production</span></h3>
<p>By April 2010, <a href="/wiki/Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon">Joss Whedon</a> was close to completing a deal to direct the film and to rework Penn's script,<sup id="cite_ref-Whedon_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whedon-63">[63]</a></sup> and was officially announced in July 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Slashfilm_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slashfilm-64">[64]</a></sup> When Whedon received Penn's draft, he told Feige he felt the studio did not "have anything" and they should "pretend this draft never happened". Whedon went on to write a five page treatment of his plan for the film, and created the tagline "Avengers: Some Assembly Required", riffing on the "Avengers Assemble" slogan from the comic books. Marvel quickly began working to sign Whedon to write and direct, only stipulating that he include the Avengers against Loki, a battle among the heroes in the middle, a battle against the villains at the end, and he get the movie done for its May 2012 release.<sup id="cite_ref-WhedonBusinessInsider_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhedonBusinessInsider-65">[65]</a></sup> On the hiring, Arad stated: "My personal opinion is that Joss will do a fantastic job. He loves these characters and is a fantastic writer... It's part of his life so you know he is going to protect it... I expect someone like him is going to make the script even better".<sup id="cite_ref-SuperheroHype3_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperheroHype3-66">[66]</a></sup> Feige added, "I've known Joss for many years. We were looking for the right thing and he came in and met on it... we want[ed] to find a director that’s on the verge of doing something great, as we think Joss is."<sup id="cite_ref-MTVNews8_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNews8-67">[67]</a></sup> Whedon stated at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a>, that what drew him to the film is that he loves how "these people shouldn't be in the same room let alone on the same team—and that is the definition of family".<sup id="cite_ref-MTVNews4_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVNews4-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Joss_Whedon_looking_right.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7d/Joss_Whedon_looking_right.jpg/220px-Joss_Whedon_looking_right.jpg" width="220" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7d/Joss_Whedon_looking_right.jpg/330px-Joss_Whedon_looking_right.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7d/Joss_Whedon_looking_right.jpg/440px-Joss_Whedon_looking_right.jpg 2x" data-file-width="463" data-file-height="597" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Joss_Whedon_looking_right.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Joss Whedon at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The casting process continued into much of 2010, with the additions of <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Renner" title="Jeremy Renner">Jeremy Renner</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Renner_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Renner-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ruffalo" title="Mark Ruffalo">Mark Ruffalo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ruffalo_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ruffalo-12">[12]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Clark_Gregg" title="Clark Gregg">Clark Gregg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gregg_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg-29">[29]</a></sup> Ruffalo replaced Edward Norton, whom Marvel declined to have back.<sup id="cite_ref-HitFix_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HitFix-69">[69]</a></sup> "We have made the decision to not bring Ed Norton back to portray the title role of Bruce Banner in <i>The Avengers</i>," stated Feige. "Our decision is definitely not one based on monetary factors, but instead rooted in the need for an actor who embodies the creativity and collaborative spirit of our other talented cast members. <i>The Avengers</i> demands players who thrive working as part of an ensemble, as evidenced by Robert, Chris H, Chris E, Samuel, Scarlett, and all of our talented casts. We are looking to announce a name actor who fulfills these requirements, and is passionate about the iconic role in the coming weeks."<sup id="cite_ref-HitFix2_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HitFix2-70">[70]</a></sup> In response, Norton's agent Brian Swardstrom decried Feige's statement, calling it "purposefully misleading" and an "inappropriate attempt to paint our client in a negative light".<sup id="cite_ref-HitFix3_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HitFix3-71">[71]</a></sup> In October 2014, Norton claimed it was his own decision never to play Hulk again because he "wanted more diversity" with his career, and did not want to be associated with only one character.<sup id="cite_ref-NortonTHR_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NortonTHR-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2010, it was reported that Paramount Pictures and Marvel Studios were planning to start shooting in February.<sup id="cite_ref-SuperheroHype4_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperheroHype4-73">[73]</a></sup> Simultaneously, it was declared that the film would be shot in 3D,<sup id="cite_ref-Showbiz411_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Showbiz411-74">[74]</a></sup> although Mark Ruffalo later <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeted</a> that this was not the case.<sup id="cite_ref-Mruff221_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mruff221-75">[75]</a></sup> In October 2010, <a href="/wiki/Grumman_Studios" title="Grumman Studios">Grumman Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bethpage,_New_York" title="Bethpage, New York">Bethpage, New York</a><sup id="cite_ref-LIBN_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LIBN-76">[76]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Steiner_Studios" title="Steiner Studios">Steiner Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York City, were announced as filming locations,<sup id="cite_ref-NewsdayGrumman_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewsdayGrumman-77">[77]</a></sup> with set construction slated to begin in November,<sup id="cite_ref-LIBN_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LIBN-76">[76]</a></sup> but as Whedon later explained, "Originally we were supposed to be in Los Angeles, then for a short period we were supposed to be in New York, and then somehow we ended up in Albuquerque."<sup id="cite_ref-filmfestivaltraveler_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmfestivaltraveler-4">[4]</a></sup> Also that October, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a> agreed to pay Paramount at least $115&#160;million for the worldwide distribution rights to <i>Iron Man&#160;3</i> and <i>The Avengers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Variety2_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety2-78">[78]</a></sup> The deal also allowed Paramount to continue to collect the 8&#160;percent box office fee it would have earned for distributing the film and a marquee credit—placement of the company's <a href="/wiki/Production_logo" title="Production logo">production logo</a> on marketing materials and the film's opening titles. As a result, the onscreen production credit reads "Marvel Studios presents in association with Paramount Pictures" though the film is solely owned, distributed, financed, and marketed by Disney. Paramount's <a href="/wiki/Epix_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="Epix (TV network)">Epix</a> retained pay TV rights.<sup id="cite_ref-Variety4_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety4-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2010, Governor of New Mexico <a href="/wiki/Bill_Richardson" title="Bill Richardson">Bill Richardson</a> and Marvel Studios Co-president Louis D'Esposito announced <i>The Avengers</i> would film primarily in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque, New Mexico</a>, with principal photography scheduled for April through September 2011. Parts of the film were also scheduled to be shot in Michigan,<sup id="cite_ref-FilmNewMexico_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FilmNewMexico-80">[80]</a></sup> but a plan to film in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> ended after Governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Snyder" title="Rick Snyder">Rick Snyder</a> issued a budget proposal that would eliminate a film tax incentive.<sup id="cite_ref-DetroitFreePress_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DetroitFreePress-81">[81]</a></sup> Three months later in March, Governor of Ohio <a href="/wiki/John_Kasich" title="John Kasich">John Kasich</a> announced before Mayor <a href="/wiki/Frank_G._Jackson" title="Frank G. Jackson">Frank G. Jackson</a>'s State of the City address that <i>The Avengers</i> would film in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cleveland_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cleveland-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Concept illustrator and designer of Iron Man's Mark VII armor Phil Saunders stated that "Joss Whedon was looking for something that had the 'cool' factor of the suitcase suit [from <i>Iron Man 2</i>], while still being a fully armored, heavy duty suit that could take on an army in the final battle." To that end, Saunders borrowed ideas that had been proposed in <i>Iron Man&#160;2</i> as well as some ideas that had been abandoned in <i>Iron Man</i> and merged them together in a modular suit that has big ammo packets on the arms and a backpack.<sup id="cite_ref-Marvel4_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marvel4-83">[83]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Science_%26_Entertainment_Exchange" title="Science &amp; Entertainment Exchange">Science &amp; Entertainment Exchange</a> also provided science consultation for the film.<sup id="cite_ref-SEE_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEE-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Casting reached its final stages the following year. In February 2011, <a href="/wiki/Cobie_Smulders" title="Cobie Smulders">Cobie Smulders</a> acquired the role of Maria Hill,<sup id="cite_ref-Variety3_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety3-34">[34]</a></sup> after participating in screen tests conducted by Marvel for the role of a key S.H.I.E.L.D. member, who Samuel L. Jackson described as Nick Fury's sidekick.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter3_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter3-33">[33]</a></sup> Over the successive months, the film's cast expanded to include <a href="/wiki/Stellan_Skarsg%C3%A5rd" title="Stellan Skarsgård">Stellan Skarsgård</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Expressen_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Expressen-37">[37]</a></sup> Paul Bettany,<sup id="cite_ref-Bettany_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bettany-85">[85]</a></sup> and Gwyneth Paltrow.<sup id="cite_ref-PaltrowPossibly_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PaltrowPossibly-86">[86]</a></sup> Paltrow was cast at Downey's insistence; prior to this, Whedon had not intended the film to include supporting characters from the heroes' individual films, commenting, "You need to separate the characters from their support systems in order to create the isolation you need for a team."<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes3_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes3-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Avengers_on_E_9th.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Avengers_on_E_9th.jpg/200px-Avengers_on_E_9th.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Avengers_on_E_9th.jpg/300px-Avengers_on_E_9th.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Avengers_on_E_9th.jpg/400px-Avengers_on_E_9th.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1360" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Part of <i>The Avengers</i> film set on East 9th Street in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, Ohio.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Avengers_Park_Avenue_film_set.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Avengers_Park_Avenue_film_set.jpg/200px-Avengers_Park_Avenue_film_set.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Avengers_Park_Avenue_film_set.jpg/300px-Avengers_Park_Avenue_film_set.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Avengers_Park_Avenue_film_set.jpg/400px-Avengers_Park_Avenue_film_set.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Part of <i>The Avengers</i> film set on <a href="/wiki/Park_Avenue" title="Park Avenue">Park Avenue</a> in New York City.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> began on April 25, 2011, in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque" class="mw-redirect" title="Albuquerque">Albuquerque</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Filming_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Filming-88">[88]</a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/Working_title" title="Working title">working title</a> <i>Group Hug</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-WorkingTitle_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorkingTitle-89">[89]</a></sup> In June 2011, stuntman Jeremy Fitzgerald injured his head while attempting a stunt involving a 30-foot fall from a building after getting hit by an arrow. A Marvel spokesperson later told <a href="/wiki/TMZ_(website)" class="mw-redirect" title="TMZ (website)">TMZ.com</a> that despite the injury, Fitzgerald recovered and continued working on set.<sup id="cite_ref-TMZ_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMZ-90">[90]</a></sup> The following month, <a href="/wiki/Second_unit" title="Second unit">secondary filming</a> took place about an hour outside <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, Pennsylvania in the <a href="/wiki/Butler_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Butler County, Pennsylvania">Butler area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vancheri_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vancheri-91">[91]</a></sup> A chase sequence was also shot in <a href="/wiki/Worthington,_Pennsylvania" title="Worthington, Pennsylvania">Worthington, Pennsylvania</a> at Creekside Mushroom Farms, the world's largest single-site mushroom farm, which provided 150 miles of abandoned limestone tunnels 300 feet below the ground for filming.<sup id="cite_ref-Vancheri2_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vancheri2-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Production relocated to Cleveland, Ohio in August 2011, where filming transpired over a period of four weeks. The city's East 9th Street was chosen as a double for New York City's <a href="/wiki/42nd_Street_(Manhattan)" title="42nd Street (Manhattan)">42nd Street</a> to be used in climactic battle scenes.<sup id="cite_ref-Sangiacomo_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sangiacomo-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Reserve" title="United States Army Reserve">Army Reserve</a> soldiers assigned to the <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>-based <a href="/wiki/200th_Military_Police_Command_(United_States)" title="200th Military Police Command (United States)">391st Military Police Battalion</a> provided background action during the battle scenes in Cleveland. Staff Sergeant Michael T. Landis stated the use of real soldiers made the scenes more realistic and helped portray the military in a more positive light, explaining that, "It's easy for us to make on-the-spot corrections to tactics and uniforms, the director actually took our recommendation on one scene and let us all engage the enemy as opposed to only the gunners in the trucks engaging".<sup id="cite_ref-Army_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Army-94">[94]</a></sup> Filming also took place in the large <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_chamber" title="Vacuum chamber">vacuum chamber</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Research_Center" title="Glenn Research Center">NASA Plum Brook Station</a> near <a href="/wiki/Sandusky,_Ohio" title="Sandusky, Ohio">Sandusky, Ohio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sandusky_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sandusky-95">[95]</a></sup> The station's <a href="/wiki/Space_Power_Facility" title="Space Power Facility">Space Power Facility</a> was used to portray a S.H.I.E.L.D. research facility.<sup id="cite_ref-Sandusky2_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sandusky2-96">[96]</a></sup> A series of explosions were filmed at the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> powertrain plant in <a href="/wiki/Parma,_Ohio" title="Parma, Ohio">Parma, Ohio</a> as part of the battle sequence that began in Cleveland.<sup id="cite_ref-Sangiacomo2_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sangiacomo2-97">[97]</a></sup> Scenes from the film were also shot on <a href="/wiki/Public_Square,_Cleveland" title="Public Square, Cleveland">Public Square</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Detroit%E2%80%93Superior_Bridge" title="Detroit–Superior Bridge">Detroit–Superior Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sangiacomo3_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sangiacomo3-98">[98]</a></sup> Public Square's southwest quadrant was turned into Stuttgart, Germany, for filming.<sup id="cite_ref-Sangiacomo4_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sangiacomo4-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>Principal photography concluded in New York City, where filming occurred over two days.<sup id="cite_ref-Sangiacomo5_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sangiacomo5-100">[100]</a></sup> Filming locations in New York City included <a href="/wiki/Park_Avenue" title="Park Avenue">Park Avenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SuperheroHype5_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperheroHype5-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DailyMail_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyMail-102">[102]</a></sup> For scenes taking place in Manhattan, visual effects supervisor Jake Morrison shot aerial footage for over three days to use as background plates, elaborating that his main objective was to "get as much aerial work in as possible for the audience to see the big expanses, the wide establishing shots, while also making sure that the effects work doesn't look too computer generated".<sup id="cite_ref-ARRI1_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARRI1-103">[103]</a></sup> "We're getting much better at making entirely computer-generated environments," Morrison explained, "but there is no substitute for starting with a real image and adding what you need."<sup id="cite_ref-ARRI1_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARRI1-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cinematographer <a href="/wiki/Seamus_McGarvey" title="Seamus McGarvey">Seamus McGarvey</a> stated that he composed the frame with a 1.85:1 <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio_(image)" title="Aspect ratio (image)">aspect ratio</a> to cope with the varying heights of the main characters, explaining that "shooting 1.85:1 is kind of unusual for an epic film like this, but we needed the height in the screen to be able to frame in all the characters like Hulk, Captain America and Black Widow, who is much smaller. We had to give them all precedence and width within the frame. Also, Joss [Whedon] knew the final battle sequence was going to be this extravaganza in Manhattan, so the height and vertical scale of the buildings was going to be really important."<sup id="cite_ref-ARRI2_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARRI2-104">[104]</a></sup> The film was McGarvey's first venture shooting with a digital camera, the <a href="/wiki/Arri_Alexa" title="Arri Alexa">Arri Alexa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ARRI2_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARRI2-104">[104]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Canon_EOS_5D_Mark_II" title="Canon EOS 5D Mark II">Canon EOS 5D Mark II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canon_EOS_7D" title="Canon EOS 7D">Canon EOS 7D</a> <a href="/wiki/Digital_single-lens_reflex_camera" title="Digital single-lens reflex camera">digital SLR cameras</a> were used for some shots,<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter13_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter13-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Canon7D_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canon7D-106">[106]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/High-speed_photography" title="High-speed photography">high-speed</a> shots were captured on <a href="/wiki/35_mm_film" title="35 mm film">35 mm film</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Arriflex_435" title="Arriflex 435">Arriflex 435</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ARRI2_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARRI2-104">[104]</a></sup> About his visual approach, McGarvey remarked, "Joss and I were keen on having a very visceral and naturalistic quality to the image. We wanted this to feel immersive and did not want a 'comic book look' that might distance an audience with the engagement of the film. We moved the camera a lot on Steadicam, cranes and on dollies to create kinetic images; and we chose angles that were dramatic, like low angles for heroic imagery."<sup id="cite_ref-ARRI2_104-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARRI2-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-production">Post-production</span></h3>
<p>In December 2011, Disney announced that the film would be <a href="/wiki/2D_to_3D_conversion" title="2D to 3D conversion">converted</a> to 3D.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline2_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline2-107">[107]</a></sup> Said Whedon, "I'm not a big fan of extreme long lens, talky movies – I like to see the space I'm in and relate to it, so 3D kinda fits my aesthetic anyway. And the technology has advanced so far in the past couple years." Whedon also said that "there definitely are movies that shouldn't be in 3D" but "<i>The Avengers</i> isn't obnoxiously 3D. There's no, 'Oh look, we're going to spend 20 minutes going through this tunnel because it's in 3D!' And no one is pointing at the screen the entire time. But it's an action movie. Things tend to hurtle toward the screen anyway".<sup id="cite_ref-Sampson_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sampson-108">[108]</a></sup> In January 2012, it was reported that the film would be digitally remastered for <a href="/wiki/IMAX_3D" class="mw-redirect" title="IMAX 3D">IMAX 3D</a> and open in IMAX theaters on May 4, 2012, the same day it opens in regular theaters. The film's IMAX release follows Marvel's IMAX releases of <i>Iron Man 2</i> and <i>Thor</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMAX_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMAX-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a May 2012 interview, Whedon said that it was his decision to include Thanos in a post-credits scene, although the character is not identified in the film. "He for me is the most powerful and fascinating Marvel villain. He's the great grand daddy of the badasses and he's in love with <a href="/wiki/Death_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Death (Marvel Comics)">Death</a> and I just think that's so cute. For me, the greatest Avengers [comic book] was <i>Avengers Annual</i> #7 (1977) that <a href="/wiki/Jim_Starlin" title="Jim Starlin">Jim Starlin</a> did followed by <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_Two-in-One" title="Marvel Two-in-One">Marvel Two-in-One Annual</a></i> #2 (1977) that contained the death of <a href="/wiki/Adam_Warlock" title="Adam Warlock">Adam Warlock</a>. Those were some of the most important texts and I think underrated milestones in Marvel history and Thanos is all over that, so somebody had to be in control and had to be behind Loki's work and I was like 'It's got to be Thanos.' And they said 'Okay' and I'm like 'Oh my God!'"<sup id="cite_ref-Thanos_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thanos-110">[110]</a></sup> An additional coda involving the Avengers eating shawarma was shot on April 12, 2012, a day after the world premiere.<sup id="cite_ref-EW_post-credits_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW_post-credits-111">[111]</a></sup> Shawarma sales in Los Angeles, St. Louis, and Boston reportedly skyrocketed in the days following the film's release.<sup id="cite_ref-Shawarma1_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shawarma1-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shawarma2_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shawarma2-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shawarma3_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shawarma3-114">[114]</a></sup> Whedon stated the inspiration for the shawarma scene came from the events surrounding the filming of the scene where <a href="/wiki/Winifred_Burkle" title="Winifred Burkle">Fred</a> dies in <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Wyndam-Pryce" title="Wesley Wyndam-Pryce">Wesley</a>'s arms in the <i><a href="/wiki/Angel_(1999_TV_series)" title="Angel (1999 TV series)">Angel</a></i> episode, "<a href="/wiki/A_Hole_in_the_World" title="A Hole in the World">A Hole in the World</a>". After filming the scene, Whedon and actors <a href="/wiki/Amy_Acker" title="Amy Acker">Amy Acker</a> and Denisof, who portrayed Fred and Wesley, respectively, "went out for drinks and ended up just sitting around quietly, exhausted from the day's events," which Whedon then mimicked in the scene for the film.<sup id="cite_ref-ShawarmaAngelInspiration_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShawarmaAngelInspiration-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hulk_mocap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Hulk_mocap.jpg/220px-Hulk_mocap.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/47/Hulk_mocap.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="167" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hulk_mocap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mark Ruffalo as the Hulk (bottom) wearing a <a href="/wiki/Motion_capture" title="Motion capture">motion capture</a> suit and prosthetics on his upper half to simulate the Hulk's size<sup id="cite_ref-ScreenCrush_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScreenCrush-116">[116]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The film contains more than 2,200 visual effects shots completed by 14 companies: <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">Industrial Light &amp; Magic</a> (ILM), <a href="/wiki/Weta_Digital" title="Weta Digital">Weta Digital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scanline_VFX" title="Scanline VFX">Scanline VFX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydraulx" title="Hydraulx">Hydraulx</a>, Fuel VFX, Evil Eye Pictures, <a href="/wiki/Luma_Pictures" title="Luma Pictures">Luma Pictures</a>, Cantina Creative, Trixter, <a href="/wiki/Modus_FX" title="Modus FX">Modus FX</a>, Whiskytree, <a href="/wiki/Digital_Domain" title="Digital Domain">Digital Domain</a>, The Third Floor and Method Design. ILM was the lead vendor and shared responsibility for creating many of the film's key effects, including the Helicarrier, the New York cityscape, digital body doubles, Iron Man and the Hulk. To create the on-screen Hulk, Ruffalo performed in a motion-capture suit on set with the other actors while four motion-capture HD cameras (two full body, two focused on his face) captured his face and body movements.<sup id="cite_ref-fxguide_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-117">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeff_White_(visual_effects)" title="Jeff White (visual effects)">Jeff White</a>, ILM's visual effects supervisor, said, "We really wanted to utilize everything we've developed the last 10 years and make it a pretty spectacular Hulk. One of the great design decisions was to incorporate Mark Ruffalo into the look of him. So, much of Hulk is based on Ruffalo and his performance, not only in motion capture and on set, but down to his eyes, his teeth, and his tongue."<sup id="cite_ref-AWN_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AWN-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>ILM digitally recreated the vast majority of the New York cityscape used in the film. In total, ILM artists rendered an area of about ten city blocks by about four city blocks. To do this, ILM sent out a team of four photographers to take pictures of the area in a shoot that lasted 8 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-fxguide_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-117">[117]</a></sup> Disney and <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures" title="Sony Pictures">Sony Pictures</a> agreed for <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">OsCorp</a> Tower from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(2012_film)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film)">The Amazing Spider-Man</a></i> to be included in the film, but the idea was dropped because much of the skyline had already been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-latino-review_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latino-review-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>Weta Digital took over duties for animating Iron Man during the forest duel from ILM. Guy Williams, Weta's visual effects supervisor, said, "We shared assets back and forth with ILM, but our pipelines are unique and it's hard for other assets to plug into it. But in this case, we got their models and we had to redo the texture spaces because the way we texture maps is different."<sup id="cite_ref-AWN_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AWN-118">[118]</a></sup> Williams said the most difficult part was re-creating Iron Man's reflective metal surfaces.<sup id="cite_ref-fxguide_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Scanline VFX completed the reveal shots of the Helicarrier, from the moment Black Widow and Captain America arrive on the carrier deck to the point where it lifts off. Evil Eye Pictures composited digital backgrounds into shots filmed against a greenscreen for scenes taking place inside the Helicarrier. Colin Strause of Hydraulx said, "We did the opening ten minutes of the movie, other than the opening set-up in space" including Loki's arrival on Earth and subsequent escape from the S.H.I.E.L.D. base. Luma Pictures worked on shots featuring the Helicarrier's bridge and incorporated the graphic monitor displays that were developed by Cantina Creative. Fuel VFX completed shots taking place in and around Tony Stark's penthouse at Stark Tower. Digital Domain created the asteroid environment, where Loki encounters The Other.<sup id="cite_ref-fxguide_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fxguide-117">[117]</a></sup> Method Design in Los Angeles created the film's closing credits. Steve Viola, creative director at Method Design, said, "This piece was a two-minute, self-contained main on end sequence created entirely in CG. For each of the shots in the sequence, we designed, modeled, textured, and lit all of the environments and many of the foreground objects. We received assets from Marvel to include in the piece, then heavily re-modeled and re-surfaced them to create a post-battle macro sequence. We also designed a custom typeface for the Main Title of <i>The Avengers</i> as well as 30 credits set in-scene."<sup id="cite_ref-AWN_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AWN-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(soundtrack)" title="The Avengers (soundtrack)">The Avengers (soundtrack)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Music of the Marvel Cinematic Universe">Music of the Marvel Cinematic Universe</a></div>
<p>In November 2011, Marvel announced that <a href="/wiki/Alan_Silvestri" title="Alan Silvestri">Alan Silvestri</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">scored</a> <i>Captain America: The First Avenger</i>, would write and compose the score for <i>The Avengers</i>. Silvestri said, "I've worked on films where there have been a number of stars and certainly worked on films where there have been characters of equal weight in terms of their level of importance and profile in the film, but this one is somewhat extreme in that regard because each of these characters has their own world and it's a very different situation. It's very challenging to look for a way to give everyone the weight and consideration they need, but at the same time the film is really about the coming together of these characters, which implies that there is this entity called the Avengers which really has to be representative of all of them together."<sup id="cite_ref-Silvestri_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silvestri-120">[120]</a></sup> Silvestri developed the score with the <a href="/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra" title="London Symphony Orchestra">London Symphony Orchestra</a> at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a> in London, England.<sup id="cite_ref-SXSW1_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SXSW1-121">[121]</a></sup> Whedon said, "The score is very old-fashioned, which is why [Silvestri] was letter-perfect for this movie because he can give you the heightened emotion, the [<a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a>] school of 'I'm just feeling a lot right now!' but he can also be extraordinarily cue and character specific, which I love."<sup id="cite_ref-SXSW1_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SXSW1-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
