<p>In March 2012, American <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Soundgarden" title="Soundgarden">Soundgarden</a> announced through its Facebook page that its song "<a href="/wiki/Live_to_Rise" title="Live to Rise">Live to Rise</a>" would be included on the film's soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-Soundgarden_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soundgarden-122">[122]</a></sup> Additionally, the Indian rock band <a href="/wiki/Agnee_(band)" title="Agnee (band)">Agnee</a> released a music video for its single "Hello Andheron", which serves as the theme song for the film's Indian release.<sup id="cite_ref-Agnee_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agnee-123">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Records" title="Hollywood Records">Hollywood Records</a> released the soundtrack <a href="/wiki/Concept_album" title="Concept album">concept album</a> inspired by the film, <i>Avengers Assemble</i>, on May 1, 2012, the same day as the score.<sup id="cite_ref-Soundtrack_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soundtrack-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg/220px-Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg/330px-Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg/440px-Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fans_at_Avengers_premiere.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fans at the film's world premiere, outside Hollywood's <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 2012, Disney announced that the film's title would be changed in the United Kingdom to avoid confusion with the <a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(TV_series)" title="The Avengers (TV series)">British TV series of the same name</a>, as well as its <a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(1998_film)" title="The Avengers (1998 film)">1998 film adaptation</a>. This led to confusion over the film's actual title. <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine reported that the film would be titled <i>Marvel Avengers Assemble</i><sup id="cite_ref-AvengersAssemble2_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvengersAssemble2-125">[125]</a></sup> while <i>The Hollywood Reporter</i> said that it would be called simply <i>Avengers Assemble</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-AvengersAssemble_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvengersAssemble-126">[126]</a></sup> Marvel's UK website refers to the film as <i>Marvel's Avengers Assemble</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-MarvelUK_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarvelUK-127">[127]</a></sup> although David Cox of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, in arguing that it was one of the worst film titles ever, considered this to be an error in the production notes, albeit grammatically clearer.<sup id="cite_ref-Cox_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox-128">[128]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/British_Board_of_Film_Classification" title="British Board of Film Classification">British Board of Film Classification</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Film_Classification_Office" title="Irish Film Classification Office">Irish Film Classification Office</a>, the title is <i>Marvel Avengers Assemble</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBFC_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBFC-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IFCO_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFCO-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lovece" title="Frank Lovece">Frank Lovece</a> in FilmFestivalTraveler.com addressed the discrepancy, writing, "<i>The Avengers</i> — formally titled <i>Marvel's The Avengers</i> onscreen, though no apostrophe-s appears on the posters..."<sup id="cite_ref-filmfestivaltraveler_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmfestivaltraveler-4">[4]</a></sup> Producer Kevin Feige said there are only two words in the UK title, one more than in the U.S. title, and stated that "decisions like that aren't made lightly and there are lots of marketing research, lawyers and things that get into the mix on it".<sup id="cite_ref-digitalspy_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitalspy-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The film's world premiere was April 11, 2012, at Hollywood's <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-premiere_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-130">[130]</a></sup> <i>The Avengers</i> closed the 11th Annual <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a> with a screening on April 28, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Tribeca_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tribeca-131">[131]</a></sup> The film received an expanded one-week theatrical push for the 2012 U.S. <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a> weekend, increasing the number of theaters from 123 to 1,700.<sup id="cite_ref-LaborDayPush_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaborDayPush-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h3>
<p>The film was promoted at the 2010 San Diego Comic-Con International, during which a teaser trailer narrated by Samuel L. Jackson was shown followed by an introduction of the cast.<sup id="cite_ref-Gregg_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg-29">[29]</a></sup> In June 2011, Marvel Studios announced that it would not hold a panel at the 2011 San Diego Comic-Con International after studio executives decided it was not prepared to compete with its own past and fan expectations with filming still in production.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes-133">[133]</a></sup> In July 2011, a teaser trailer that was meant to be the post-credits scene of <i>Captain America: The First Avenger</i> was briefly leaked online. <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> speculated it came from a preview screening and described the footage as "shaky, fuzzy, flickering and obviously filmed on a cell phone".<sup id="cite_ref-EW3_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW3-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20111015_NYCC-6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/20111015_NYCC-6.jpg/220px-20111015_NYCC-6.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/20111015_NYCC-6.jpg/330px-20111015_NYCC-6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/20111015_NYCC-6.jpg/440px-20111015_NYCC-6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1060" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20111015_NYCC-6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chris Evans, Tom Hiddleston, Cobie Smulders, and Clark Gregg promoting the film at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/New_York_Comic_Con" title="New York Comic Con">New York Comic Con</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In August 2011, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pixar_Animation_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Pixar Animation Studios">Pixar Animation Studios</a> and Marvel Studios presented a look at <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a>' upcoming film slate, which included <i>The Avengers</i>, at the <a href="/wiki/D23_Expo" class="mw-redirect" title="D23 Expo">D23 Expo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>. The presentation featured footage from the film and appearances by the cast members.<sup id="cite_ref-D23_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D23-135">[135]</a></sup> Later in August, Disney dismissed Marvel's executive vice president of worldwide marketing, vice president of worldwide marketing and manager of worldwide marketing to bring their functions <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Marketing" title="Walt Disney Studios Marketing">in-house</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2011, Marvel Studios held a presentation at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Comic_Con" title="New York Comic Con">New York Comic Con</a> that featured new footage and a panel discussion including producer Kevin Feige and several cast members.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCC_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCC-137">[137]</a></sup> The first full-length trailer was also released in October. <i><a href="/wiki/Comic_Book_Resources" title="Comic Book Resources">Comic Book Resources</a></i> said, "The two-minute teaser handily establishes the movie's premise" and is "heavy on the assembling, but fans are also treated to plenty of action, as well glimpses  [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] of Iron Man's new armor and, best of all, the new take on the Incredible Hulk. Naturally, Robert Downey Jr.'s Tony Stark gets the best lines".<sup id="cite_ref-CBR_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBR-138">[138]</a></sup> However, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> called it, "Awesome. Or it would be if we hadn't seen all of this before and expected every single thing that we saw in the trailer".<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter6_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter6-139">[139]</a></sup> The trailer, which debuted exclusively on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes Movie Trailers</a>, was downloaded over 10&#160;million times in its first 24 hours, breaking the website's record for the most-viewed trailer.<sup id="cite_ref-BusinessWire_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusinessWire-140">[140]</a></sup> This record was surpassed by the trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i>, which was downloaded more than 12.5&#160;million times in its first 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-MarketWatch_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarketWatch-141">[141]</a></sup> The trailer received 20.4 million views in the 24 hours after it debuted.<sup id="cite_ref-TrailerViews_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TrailerViews-142">[142]</a></sup> A second full-length trailer was released on iTunes in February 2012, reaching a record 13.7&#160;million downloads in 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-NYDailyNews_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYDailyNews-143">[143]</a></sup> The theatrical trailers of <i>The Avengers</i> appeared with many films, including <i><a href="/wiki/Mission:_Impossible_%E2%80%93_Ghost_Protocol" title="Mission: Impossible – Ghost Protocol">Mission: Impossible – Ghost Protocol</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/21_Jump_Street_(film)" title="21 Jump Street (film)">21 Jump Street</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_Games_(film)" title="The Hunger Games (film)">The Hunger Games</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline5_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline5-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2012, Marvel Studios held a global Twitter chat. The 30-minute live tweeting event featured writer/director Joss Whedon, cast members Samuel L. Jackson, Tom Hiddleston and Clark Gregg and a 10-second tease of the 30-second <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> commercial that would air during <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl XLVI</a> in February.<sup id="cite_ref-Marvel2_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marvel2-145">[145]</a></sup> According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, Disney paid an estimated $4&#160;million for the 30-second spot.<sup id="cite_ref-Fritz_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fritz-146">[146]</a></sup> On May 1, 2012, executives from Marvel Studios, along with actors Tom Hiddleston and Clark Gregg, rang the opening bell of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> in honor of the film's theatrical release.<sup id="cite_ref-NYSE_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYSE-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tie-in_comics">Tie-in comics</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_tie-in_comics" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics">Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics</a></div>
<p>In December 2011, Marvel announced that an eight-issue comic-book prelude to the film, written by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Yost" title="Christopher Yost">Christopher Yost</a> and Eric Pearson with art by <a href="/wiki/Luke_Ross" title="Luke Ross">Luke Ross</a> and Daniel HDR, would be released in March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Marvel1_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marvel1-148">[148]</a></sup> In February 2012, Marvel announced the release of a second limited series comic book tie-in, <i>Black Widow Strikes</i> written by <a href="/wiki/Fred_Van_Lente" title="Fred Van Lente">Fred Van Lente</a>, who wrote <i>Captain America: First Vengeance</i>, the comic-book prequel to <i>Captain America: The First Avenger</i>. The story is set between <i>Iron Man 2</i> and <i>The Avengers</i> and follows Black Widow as she runs down some loose ends from <i>Iron Man 2</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Marvel3_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marvel3-149">[149]</a></sup> Additionally, the title <i>Avengers Assemble</i> was launched in March 2012, written by Brian Michael Bendis with art by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Bagley" title="Mark Bagley">Mark Bagley</a> and features the same Avengers line-up as the film battling a new incarnation of the supervillain team <a href="/wiki/Zodiac_(comics)" title="Zodiac (comics)">Zodiac</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Schedeen_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schedeen-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotional_partners">Promotional partners</span></h4>
<p>Paul Gitter, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel Entertainment</a>'s president of consumer products, commented that the build-up to the film helped strengthen retail partnerships: "Retailers have been less tolerant with [intellectual property] films, so we decided that if we started on this coordinated strategy several years ago, retailers would give us shelf space throughout the years and we would have a more sustainable position in the marketplace".<sup id="cite_ref-Lisanti_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lisanti-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2011, set photos of Robert Downey Jr. driving a new model <a href="/wiki/Acura" title="Acura">Acura</a> were published online. An Acura spokesperson later released a statement confirming the company's involvement with the film, "As you may know, Acura has been in the Marvel Comics Universe films as the official car of their fictional law enforcement agency called S.H.I.E.L.D. That relationship continues for <i>The Avengers</i>. The open-top sports car that was photographed yesterday is a one-off, fictional car that was made just for the movie and will not be produced. That said, as you may also know, our CEO has said publicly that we are studying the development of a new sportscar, but we can't say any more about it at this time."<sup id="cite_ref-Nunez_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nunez-152">[152]</a></sup> In December 2011, Acura announced that a new <a href="/wiki/Honda_NSX" title="Honda NSX">NSX</a> styled along the lines of the <a href="/wiki/Concept_car" title="Concept car">concept</a> built for <i>The Avengers</i> would be unveiled at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/North_American_International_Auto_Show" title="North American International Auto Show">North American International Auto Show</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vijayenthiran_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vijayenthiran-153">[153]</a></sup> A series of 10 S.H.I.E.L.D. <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUVs</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Acura_MDX" title="Acura MDX">Acura MDX</a> with modifications by Cinema Vehicle Services, were also made for the film.<sup id="cite_ref-MDX_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MDX-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2012, it was announced that Marvel has partnered with fragrance company JADS to promote <i>The Avengers</i> with character-based fragrances. The announcement was just ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Toy_Industry_Association" title="Toy Industry Association">Toy Industry Association</a>'s annual February exhibition, where representatives held a sampling booth of the products.<sup id="cite_ref-JADS_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JADS-155">[155]</a></sup> Other promotional partners include bracelet-maker Colantotte, <a href="/wiki/Dr_Pepper" title="Dr Pepper">Dr Pepper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farmers_Insurance_Group" title="Farmers Insurance Group">Farmers Insurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harley-Davidson" title="Harley-Davidson">Harley-Davidson</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hershey_Company" title="The Hershey Company">Hershey</a>, Land O'Frost <a href="/wiki/Cold_cut" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold cut">lunchmeats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schwan_Food_Company#Red_Baron_Squadron" title="Schwan Food Company">Red Baron pizza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Symantec" title="Symantec">Symantec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wyndham_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Wyndham Hotels &amp; Resorts">Wyndham Hotels &amp; Resorts</a>. In total, Marvel and its parent-company Disney secured an estimated $100&#160;million in worldwide marketing support for the film. Notable exclusions include <a href="/wiki/Baskin-Robbins" title="Baskin-Robbins">Baskin-Robbins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts" title="Dunkin' Donuts">Dunkin' Donuts</a>, who had partnered with Marvel in the past when their films were distributed by Paramount. Disney does not generally promote through <a href="/wiki/Fast_food" title="Fast food">fast food</a> outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-Variety5_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety5-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_game">Video game</span></h4>
<p>A video game based on the film was planned for concurrent release. The game was to be a <a href="/wiki/First-person_shooter" title="First-person shooter">first-person shooter</a>/<a href="/wiki/Beat_%27em_up" title="Beat 'em up">brawler</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and published by <a href="/wiki/THQ" title="THQ">THQ</a>, with <a href="/wiki/THQ_Studio_Australia" title="THQ Studio Australia">THQ Studio Australia</a> developing the console versions and <a href="/wiki/Blue_Tongue_Entertainment" title="Blue Tongue Entertainment">Blue Tongue Entertainment</a> the <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">PC</a> version. After THQ closed both studios, the game was cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-Lien_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lien-157">[157]</a></sup> Intellectual property rights for an Avengers video game reverted to Marvel, which said it was exploring potential publishing and licensing opportunities.<sup id="cite_ref-Sinclair_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sinclair-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ubisoft" title="Ubisoft">Ubisoft</a> and Marvel Entertainment announced that they were partnering to develop a motion-controlled game titled <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_Avengers:_Battle_for_Earth" title="Marvel Avengers: Battle for Earth">Marvel Avengers: Battle for Earth</a></i> for the Wii U and Xbox 360 <a href="/wiki/Kinect" title="Kinect">Kinect</a>. The game was inspired by the "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Invasion" title="Secret Invasion">Secret Invasion</a>" storyline and features 20 different characters.<sup id="cite_ref-BfE_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BfE-159">[159]</a></sup> Marvel also announced a four-chapter <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile game</a> titled <i>Avengers Initiative</i>, with one chapter focusing on each of Hulk, Captain America, Thor and Iron Man.<sup id="cite_ref-MobileGame_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MobileGame-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span></h3>
<p>The film was released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment</a><sup id="cite_ref-HM_Magazine1_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HM_Magazine1-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bluray6_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray6-162">[162]</a></sup> on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_3D" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray 3D">Blu-ray 3D</a>, <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> and <a href="/wiki/Digital_copy" title="Digital copy">digital download</a> on September 25, 2012 in the United States and as early as August 29, 2012 in various international markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Bluray_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray-163">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bluray5_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray5-164">[164]</a></sup> Producer Kevin Feige said the Blu-ray features a new <a href="/wiki/Marvel_One-Shots" title="Marvel One-Shots">Marvel One-Shot</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Item_47" title="Item 47">Item 47</a></i> and "a number of deleted scenes and a few storylines that fell by the wayside during the editing process" including "a few more scenes with the S.H.I.E.L.D. agent Maria Hill, played by Cobie Smulders" and "some slightly different versions of Maria Hill and Nick Fury's interaction with the World Security Council".<sup id="cite_ref-Bluray3_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray3-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The film was also collected in a 10-disc <a href="/wiki/Box_set" title="Box set">box set</a> titled "<a href="/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films#Home_Media" title="List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films">Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One – Avengers Assembled</a>" which includes all of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films#Phase_One" title="List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films">Phase One</a> films in the Marvel Cinematic Universe.<sup id="cite_ref-Bluray2_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray2-166">[166]</a></sup> It was released on April 2, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Bluray4_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray4-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boxset_release_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boxset_release-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some fans have criticized the UK DVD and Blu-ray release for omitting Joss Whedon's audio commentary, and for altering the scene involving Phil Coulson's death from the film's theatrical version.<sup id="cite_ref-UKBluray_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKBluray-169">[169]</a></sup> Disney's UK division said the "less graphic depiction of Agent Coulson's confrontation with Loki" occurred because "[e]ach country has its own compliance issues relative to depictions of violence. Unfortunately, another region's elements were inadvertently used to create the UK in-home release".<sup id="cite_ref-UKBluray_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKBluray-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon its first week of release on home media in the U.S., the film topped the Nielsen VideoScan First Alert chart, which tracks overall disc sales, as well as the dedicated Blu-ray Disc sales chart with 72% of unit sales coming from Blu-ray, a record for a new release in which both the DVD and Blu-ray formats were released simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-Bluray6_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bluray6-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span></h3>
<p><i>The Avengers</i> grossed $623.4 million in North America and $895.5 million in other countries, for a worldwide total of $1.519 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-3">[3]</a></sup> It became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">third-highest-grossing film worldwide</a><sup id="cite_ref-third_highest_news_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-third_highest_news-170">[170]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/2012_in_film" title="2012 in film">highest-grossing 2012 film</a>. It is the highest-grossing <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic-book</a> adaptation, the highest-grossing <a href="/wiki/Superhero_film" title="Superhero film">superhero film</a> and the second-highest-grossing film ever released by Walt Disney Studios.<sup id="cite_ref-highest-Disney_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highest-Disney-171">[171]</a></sup> The film's worldwide opening of $392.5&#160;million is the fourth largest.<sup id="cite_ref-world-open_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-open-172">[172]</a></sup> <i>The Avengers</i> also became the fifth film distributed by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Disney</a> and the twelfth film overall to earn more than $1&#160;billion. It reached this milestone in 19 days, matching the record for speed previously set by <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i> and <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-1billion_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-1billion-173">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter16_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter16-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Time-1billion_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-1billion-175">[175]</a></sup> Its grosses exceeded its estimated $220&#160;million production cost 12 days after its release.<sup id="cite_ref-BoxOffice2_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoxOffice2-176">[176]</a></sup> It was the first Marvel production to generate $1 billion in ticket sales.<sup id="cite_ref-TicketSales_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TicketSales-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span></h4>
<p>The film became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States#Not_adjusted_for_inflation" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">third-highest-grossing film</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-third_highest_news_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-third_highest_news-170">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BOM-domestic_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-domestic-178">[178]</a></sup> the highest-grossing 2012 film,<sup id="cite_ref-2012films_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012films-179">[179]</a></sup> the highest-grossing film distributed by Disney,<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-Disney_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-Disney-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StarWars_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StarWars-181">[181]</a></sup> the highest-grossing superhero film and the highest-grossing film based on comics.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-3">[3]</a></sup> It opened Friday, May 4, 2012, on around 11,800 screens across 4,349 theaters, and earned $80.8&#160;million, marking the second-biggest opening and second-biggest single-day gross.<sup id="cite_ref-opngday_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opngday-182">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-snglday_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snglday-183">[183]</a></sup> The film's Friday gross included an $18.7&#160;million midnight run, a record for a superhero film<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-midnight_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-midnight-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-midnight-TDKR_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-midnight-TDKR-185">[185]</a></sup> Without midnight grosses, the film earned the largest opening-day gross ($62.1&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-opngday_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-opngday-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-singleday_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singleday-187">[187]</a></sup> It also set a Saturday- and Sunday-gross record ($69.6&#160;million and $57.1&#160;million respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-saturday_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saturday-188">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sunday_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunday-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BOM-opening_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-opening-190">[190]</a></sup> In total, it earned a total of $207,438,708 for its debut weekend, setting an <a href="/wiki/List_of_biggest_opening_weekends#Biggest_opening_weekends_in_U.S._and_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="List of biggest opening weekends">opening-weekend record</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> including an IMAX opening-weekend record of $15.3&#160;million<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter14_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter14-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EW-opening_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW-opening-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMAX-TDKR_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMAX-TDKR-194">[194]</a></sup> and a record for opening-weekend grosses originating from 3D showings ($108&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-opening_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-opening-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alice_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alice-195">[195]</a></sup> The opening-weekend audience was evenly split among those under and over the age of 25, with 60% of the audience male, 55% couples, 24% families and 21% teenagers.<sup id="cite_ref-NAAudience_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAAudience-196">[196]</a></sup> Earning $103.1&#160;million on its second weekend, the film set a record for the largest second-weekend gross.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-second_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-second-197">[197]</a></sup> Other records set by the film include the biggest weekend per-theater average for a wide release ($47,698 per theater),<sup id="cite_ref-average_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-average-198">[198]</a></sup> the fastest film to reach $100&#160;million and each additional $50&#160;million through $550&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-second_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-second-197">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BOM-records_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-records-199">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BOM-fifth_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-fifth-200">[200]</a></sup> and the largest cumulative gross through every day of release until, and including, its forty-third day (with the exception of its first day).<sup id="cite_ref-BOM_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-second_weekend_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-second_weekend-201">[201]</a></sup> It was in first place at the North American box office for three consecutive weekends.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-third_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-third-202">[202]</a></sup> The film set a record for the highest monthly share, with its $532.5 million total (through May 31, 2012) accounting for 52% of the total earnings at the North American box office during May.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-May_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-May-203">[203]</a></sup></p>

</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_North_America">Outside North America</span></h4>
<p>The film became the third-highest grossing film,<sup id="cite_ref-alltime-overseas_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alltime-overseas-213">[213]</a></sup> the highest-grossing Disney-distributed film,<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-overseas2_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-overseas2-214">[214]</a></sup> the highest-grossing 2012 film,<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-2012_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-2012-215">[215]</a></sup> and the highest-grossing superhero film.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter16_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter16-174">[174]</a></sup> It opened Wednesday, April 25, 2012, in 10 countries, earning $17.1&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline3_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline3-216">[216]</a></sup> It opened in 29 more countries on April 26 and 27, earning $73.1&#160;million in three days.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline4_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline4-217">[217]</a></sup> Through Sunday, April 29, it earned an opening-weekend total of $185.1&#160;million from 39 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-overseas_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-overseas-218">[218]</a></sup> It was in first place at the box office outside North America for four consecutive weekends.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter15_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter15-219">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter17_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter17-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter18_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter18-221">[221]</a></sup> The film set opening-day records in New Zealand, Malaysia and Iceland, a single-day record in the Philippines, as well as both single- and opening-day records in Singapore and in Thailand. It also earned the second-highest-grossing opening day in Australia ($6.2&#160;million), behind <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i>, in Mexico, in the Philippines and in Vietnam.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline5_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline5-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Deadline3_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline3-216">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Deadline4_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline4-217">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter10_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter10-222">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter11_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter11-223">[223]</a></sup> It set opening-weekend records in many territories, including Mexico, Brazil, Ecuador, Bolivia, Taiwan, the Philippines, Hong Kong, the United Arab Emirates, Argentina,<sup id="cite_ref-argentina_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-argentina-224">[224]</a></sup> Peru and Central America.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-overseas_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-overseas-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iceage4_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iceage4-225">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter12_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter12-226">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-deadline7_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deadline7-227">[227]</a></sup> It also earned the second largest five-day opening in Australia ($20.2&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-BOM-overseas_218-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-overseas-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aus-opening_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aus-opening-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the UK, Ireland and Malta, the film earned £2.5&#160;million ($4.1&#160;million) on its opening day<sup id="cite_ref-NME2_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME2-229">[229]</a></sup> and £15.8&#160;million ($25.7&#160;million) during the weekend,<sup id="cite_ref-UK-opening_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK-opening-230">[230]</a></sup> setting an opening-weekend record for a superhero film.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter11_223-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter11-223">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-digitaspy2_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitaspy2-231">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-overseas1_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overseas1-232">[232]</a></sup> It became the market's highest-grossing superhero film.<sup id="cite_ref-UK-top_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK-top-233">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TDKR-UK_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TDKR-UK-234">[234]</a></sup> In Latin America, it became the highest-grossing film ($207 million)<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter20_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter20-235">[235]</a></sup> and the first film to earn more than $200 million.<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter19_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter19-236">[236]</a></sup> It also became the highest-grossing film in the Philippines, in Singapore and in Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-boxcom-Avengers_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxcom-Avengers-237">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indonesia-im3_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indonesia-im3-238">[238]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg/220px-Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg/330px-Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/45/Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="433" data-file-height="650" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Ruffalo_at_the_Toronto_premiere_of_The_Avengers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mark_Ruffalo" title="Mark Ruffalo">Mark Ruffalo</a> at the film's Toronto premiere. Ruffalo's performance was critically lauded.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> reported a 92% approval rating with an average rating of 8/10 based on 315 reviews. The website's consensus reads, "Thanks to a script that emphasizes its heroes' humanity and a wealth of superpowered set pieces, <i>The Avengers</i> lives up to its hype and raises the bar for Marvel at the movies."<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, the film achieved an average score of 69 out of 100 based on 43 reviews, signifying "generally favorable reviews".<sup id="cite_ref-Metacritic_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-240">[240]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> reported that audiences gave the film a rare "A+" grade.<sup id="cite_ref-Crit1_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crit1-241">[241]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Todd_McCarthy" title="Todd McCarthy">Todd McCarthy</a> of <i>The Hollywood Reporter</i> gave a positive review of the film, remarking, "It's clamorous, the save-the-world story is one everyone's seen time and again, and the characters have been around for more than half a century in 500 comic book issues. But Whedon and his cohorts have managed to stir all the personalities and ingredients together so that the resulting dish, however familiar, is irresistibly tasty again."<sup id="cite_ref-HollywoodReporter9_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollywoodReporter9-242">[242]</a></sup> To <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> journalist <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a>, the film epitomized an exceptional blockbuster. "It's also the blockbuster," Travers said, "I saw in my head when I imagined a movie that brought together the idols of the Marvel world in one shiny, stupendously exciting package. It's <i>Transformers</i> with a brain, a heart and a working sense of humor."<sup id="cite_ref-rollz_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollz-243">[243]</a></sup> Justin Chang of <i>Variety</i> wrote, "Like a superior, state-of-the-art model built from reconstituted parts, Joss Whedon's buoyant, witty and robustly entertaining superhero smash-up is escapism of a sophisticated order, boasting a tonal assurance and rich reserves of humor that offset the potentially lumbering and unavoidably formulaic aspects of this 143-minute team-origin story."<sup id="cite_ref-Variety6_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety6-244">[244]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Turan" title="Kenneth Turan">Kenneth Turan</a> of the <i>Los Angeles Times</i> complimented the film's frenetic pace,<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes2_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes2-245">[245]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> commented that it "provides its fans with exactly what they desire. Whether it is exactly what they deserve is arguable".<sup id="cite_ref-Ebert_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ebert-246">[246]</a></sup> Conversely, <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> believed that "while <i>The Avengers</i> is hardly worth raging about, its failures are significant and dispiriting. The light, amusing bits cannot overcome the grinding, hectic emptiness, the bloated cynicism that is less a shortcoming of this particular film than a feature of the genre."<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>The performances of several cast members was a frequent topic in the critiques. In particular, Mark Ruffalo's portrayal of Dr. Bruce Banner/the Hulk was well-received by commentators. Joe Neumaier opined that his performance was superior to the rest of the cast; "Ruffalo is the revelation, turning Banner into a wry reservoir of calm ready to become a volcano."<sup id="cite_ref-nydaily_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydaily-248">[248]</a></sup> Similarly, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Lane" title="Anthony Lane">Anthony Lane</a> proclaimed Ruffalo's acting to be one of the film's highlights—alongside Downey.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-249">[249]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> <a href="/wiki/Karina_Longworth" title="Karina Longworth">Karina Longworth</a> concluded: "Ruffalo successfully refreshes the Hulk myth, playing Banner as an adorably bashful nerd-genius who, in contrast to the preening hunks on the team, knows better than to draw attention to himself."<sup id="cite_ref-villagevoice_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-villagevoice-250">[250]</a></sup> Travers asserted that the actor resonated a "scruffy warmth and humor" vibe,<sup id="cite_ref-rollz_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollz-243">[243]</a></sup> while Turan felt that he surpassed predecessors Edward Norton and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bana" title="Eric Bana">Eric Bana</a> in playing the character.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes2_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes2-245">[245]</a></sup> Owen Gleiberman of <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> wrote that "the smartest thing the filmmakers did was to get Mark Ruffalo to play Bruce Banner as a man so sensitive that he's at war, every moment, with himself. (The film finally solves the Hulk problem: He's a lot more fun in small doses.)"<sup id="cite_ref-EW-review_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EW-review-251">[251]</a></sup></p>
<p>Referring to Downey, Joe Morgenstein of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>—despite complimenting Downey's performance—favored his work in <i>Iron Man</i> over his acting in <i>The Avengers</i>: "His Iron Man is certainly a team player, but Mr. Downey comes to the party with two insuperable superpowers: a character of established sophistication—the industrialist/inventor Tony Stark, a sharp-tongued man of the world—and his own quicksilver presence that finds its finest expression in self-irony."<sup id="cite_ref-wsj22_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj22-252">[252]</a></sup> Neumaier praised Evans, stating that he accurately conveyed his character's internal conflicts.<sup id="cite_ref-nydaily_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydaily-248">[248]</a></sup></p>
<p>Commentators appreciated the character development and dialogue. <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> reviewer <a href="/wiki/Christy_Lemire" title="Christy Lemire">Christy Lemire</a> wrote that the script "sparkles as brightly as the special effects; these people may be wearing ridiculous costumes but they're well fleshed-out underneath."<sup id="cite_ref-associatedpress_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-associatedpress-253">[253]</a></sup> Scott suggested that certain parts of the film permeated a charm that he felt was similar to the western film <i><a href="/wiki/Rio_Bravo_(film)" title="Rio Bravo (film)">Rio Bravo</a></i> (1959).<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-247">[247]</a></sup> Longworth felt that while Whedon's script demonstrated the backstory of the characters, the film does not explore it "in a substantive way".<sup id="cite_ref-villagevoice_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-villagevoice-250">[250]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="List of accolades received by The Avengers (2012 film)">List of accolades received by The Avengers (2012 film)</a></div>
<p><i>The Avengers</i> has garnered numerous awards and nominations, including an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a> and a <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="British Academy Film Award">British Academy Film Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Special_Visual_Effects" title="BAFTA Award for Best Special Visual Effects">Best Special Visual Effects</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AcademyAwards_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AcademyAwards-254">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BAFTAAwards_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAFTAAwards-255">[255]</a></sup> The film has also been nominated for three <a href="/wiki/Critics%27_Choice_Movie_Awards" title="Critics' Choice Movie Awards">Critics' Choice Movie Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2012CriticChoice_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012CriticChoice-256">[256]</a></sup> thirteen <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">People's Choice Awards</a> (winning three),<sup id="cite_ref-PeoplesChoice_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeoplesChoice-257">[257]</a></sup> eleven <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">Teen Choice Awards</a> (winning two),<sup id="cite_ref-AccoTeenChoice_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AccoTeenChoice-258">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AccoTeenChoice2_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AccoTeenChoice2-259">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AccoTeenChoice3_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AccoTeenChoice3-260">[260]</a></sup> six <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn Awards</a> (winning four),<sup id="cite_ref-SaturnAwards_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SaturnAwards-261">[261]</a></sup> and six <a href="/wiki/VES_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="VES Awards">VES Awards</a> (winning two), as well as the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award" title="Hugo Award">Hugo Award</a> for Best Dramatic Presentation Long Form.<sup id="cite_ref-VESAwards_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VESAwards-262">[262]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequels">Sequels</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films" title="List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films">List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Avengers:_Age_of_Ultron"><i>Avengers: Age of Ultron</i></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Age_of_Ultron" title="Avengers: Age of Ultron">Avengers: Age of Ultron</a></div>
<p>A sequel, titled <i>Avengers: Age of Ultron</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-AvengersAgeofUltron_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvengersAgeofUltron-263">[263]</a></sup> written and directed by Whedon,<sup id="cite_ref-Variety-August2012_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety-August2012-264">[264]</a></sup> was released on May 1, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-THR-August2012_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THR-August2012-265">[265]</a></sup> Much of the cast returns, with the addition of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Olsen" title="Elizabeth Olsen">Elizabeth Olsen</a> as <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_Witch" title="Scarlet Witch">Scarlet Witch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Taylor-Johnson" title="Aaron Taylor-Johnson">Aaron Taylor-Johnson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Quicksilver_(comics)" title="Quicksilver (comics)">Quicksilver</a>, Paul Bettany as <a href="/wiki/Vision_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Vision (Marvel Comics)">Vision</a>, and <a href="/wiki/James_Spader" title="James Spader">James Spader</a> as <a href="/wiki/Ultron" title="Ultron">Ultron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AoUCast_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AoUCast-266">[266]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Avengers:_Infinity_War_and_its_sequel"><i>Avengers: Infinity War</i> and its sequel</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Infinity_War" title="Avengers: Infinity War">Avengers: Infinity War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Untitled_Avengers_film" title="Untitled Avengers film">Untitled Avengers film</a></div>
<p><i>Avengers: Infinity War</i> and an untitled sequel will be directed by <a href="/wiki/Russo_brothers" title="Russo brothers">Anthony and Joe Russo</a>, from a script by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Markus_%26_Stephen_McFeely" class="mw-redirect" title="Christopher Markus &amp; Stephen McFeely">Christopher Markus &amp; Stephen McFeely</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RussosIW_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RussosIW-267">[267]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MarkusMcFeely_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarkusMcFeely-268">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IWRetitle_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IWRetitle-269">[269]</a></sup> <i>Infinity War</i> is scheduled to be released on May 4, 2018, with the sequel scheduled for May 3, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-InfinityWar_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InfinityWar-270">[270]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<ol>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^</a></b></span> As part of the deal transferring the distribution rights of <i>The Avengers</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> to the <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Variety4_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety4-79">[79]</a></sup> Paramount's logo appears in the films' opening titles, promotional materials and merchandise.<sup id="cite_ref-ParamountVariety_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParamountVariety-271">[271]</a></sup> Nevertheless, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures">Walt Disney Studios Motion Pictures</a> is credited at the end of the film.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_2"><b><a href="#ref_2">^</a></b></span> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Movieline" title="Movieline">Movieline</a></i>, producer Kevin Feige stated that the Tesseract is based on the <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_Cube" title="Cosmic Cube">Cosmic Cube</a> from Marvel comics.<sup id="cite_ref-movieline_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-movieline-272">[272]</a></sup> After <i><a href="/wiki/Thor:_The_Dark_World" title="Thor: The Dark World">Thor: The Dark World</a></i>, in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/CraveOnline" title="CraveOnline">CraveOnline</a></i>, he stated that it was also the Space <a href="/wiki/Infinity_Gems" title="Infinity Gems">Infinity Stone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CraveOnline3_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CraveOnline3-273">[273]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_3"><b><a href="#ref_3">^</a></b></span> Feige confirmed in an <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcast</a> that the "master" in the post-credits scene is <a href="/wiki/Thanos" title="Thanos">Thanos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EmpirePodcast_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpirePodcast-274">[274]</a></sup></li>
</ol>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-soundworks-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-soundworks_17-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Supervising Sound Editor, Sound Designer, and Re-recording Mixer Christopher Boyes at 3:22 of video interview, <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://soundworkscollection.com/theavengers">"The Sound of the Avengers"</a>. SoundWorks Collection (Colemanfilm Media Group). 2012. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.webcitation.org/68C9nfvSB?url=http://soundworkscollection.com/theavengers">Archived</a> from the original on June 5, 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">June 5,</span> 2012</span>. <q>Finally I thought, 'I just have to work with human voices.' ... I just started playing combinations and I would give them 10 to 15 variations of roars. And Joss listened to them and came back and said, 'I like this one,' and I went back and I looked at the ingredients of what was in that one. Turned out to be Mark Ruffalo, some Lou Ferrigno and a little bit of me and two people from <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. So I led with that and I started using those combinations but changing it up. But the great thing was that Mark Ruffalo had done an incredible [unintelligible] of variety so I was always blending him in. ... Lou Ferrigno seemed to have a real knack for just who this character was. ... They were always a component of it.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Avengers+%282012+film%29&amp;rft.btitle=The+Sound+of+the+Avengers&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsoundworkscollection.com%2Ftheavengers&amp;rft.pub=SoundWorks+Collection+%28Colemanfilm+Media+Group%29&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
